                           <i>Primula veris S</i> locus gene structures and expression</h3><p>To determine whether the <i>S</i> locus gene sequences and structure are conserved in <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i>, genes previously identified at the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris S</i> locus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2734">27</a></sup> were aligned to our draft <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> thrum assembly (VT_v1) and the published <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> genome<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2750">14</a></sup>, alongside PCR analysis of <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> cDNA. This analysis facilitated the definition of <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> gene models for <i>PUM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> (MF317488) and <i>CCM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> (MF317489), and the correction of those for <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>, <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>KFB</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> (MF317487) (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig4">4b</a>). The intron-exon structures of the <i>S</i> locus genes are conserved (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig4">4b</a>; Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S4d</a>).</p><p>We show expression for all five <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris S</i> locus genes in <i>P</i>. <i>veris (Pve)</i> flowers, with PCR analysis of <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> cDNA, and analysis of available RNA-Seq data using our curated gene models (above) as a guide for alignment<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2833">14</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Huu, C. N. et al. Presence versus absence of CYP734A50 underlies the style-length dimorphism in primroses. eLife 5, e17956 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2836">28</a></sup> (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S6</a>). In the RNA-Seq dataset used for previous annotation of the published <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> genome assembly (PRJNA238546)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2849">14</a></sup>, we reveal expression for four of the five <i>S</i> locus genes: three show thrum-specific expression, and one (<i>PveCYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>) shows expression in thrum, with an extremely low number of pin flower RNA-Seq reads presumably erroneously mapped (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S6</a>). <i>PveCCM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> shows no expression in this dataset (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S6a</a>); the gene was not annotated in the published <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> genome assembly using this data, suggesting no transcript support in the previously reported single (unreplicated) RNA-Seq library at the sampled developmental stage<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2882">14</a></sup>; we therefore manually annotated this gene to enable the analyses detailed here. The above findings prompted our PCR analysis of <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> mixed-stage flower buds to confirm expression; this investigation revealed expression for all five genes (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S6b</a>). Furthermore, our analysis of available RNA-Seq reads derived from corolla tubes and styles of <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> pin and thrum flowers<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Huu, C. N. et al. Presence versus absence of CYP734A50 underlies the style-length dimorphism in primroses. eLife 5, e17956 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2902">28</a></sup> (pooled from 25 plants) (PRJNA317964) shows that all five genes are, as expected for this thrum-specific region, not expressed in pin for both these tissues; expression in one or more thrum plants serves as a positive control (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S6c</a>). <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> was previously shown absent from 200 <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> pin plants from a wild population<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2922">27</a></sup> (hence, pin RNA-Seq reads aligned to <i>PveGLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> are mapping errors). In conclusion, these analyses indicate the conserved presence and thrum-specific expression of all five <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris S</i> locus gene homologues in <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> thrum, alongside absence of expression in pin. This is consistent with the apparent hemizygosity of the region in <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> thrum (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig4">4a</a>), and further demonstrates conservation of <i>S</i> locus features between these two <i>Primula</i> species.</p><p>Larger intron lengths and increased prevalence of TEs have been associated with regions showing reduced recombination rates in some eukaryotes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Comeron, J. M. &amp; Kreitman, M. The correlation between intron length and recombination in Drosophila: dynamic equilibrium between mutational and selective forces. Genetics 156, 1175–1190 (2000)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d1397e2964">44</a></sup>. The hemizygous genetic architecture of the <i>S</i> locus appears to be a conserved feature, which defines the region as non-recombining. Therefore, in addition to the TE content analysed above (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">4a,b</a>), we investigated intron sizes at the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris S</i> locus compared to the wider genome. For this analysis, we examine all five <i>S</i> locus genes, using precise intron sizes for <i>PvGLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>PvCYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> that were previously determined using PCR and alignments to our draft <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> genome assemblies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3003">27</a></sup>; unambiguous sequence across corresponding introns is not available for <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i>. We previously reported the large introns of <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> in <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris (Pv)</i>; <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> spans 25 kb with two introns over 10 kb; <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> spans 68 kb with 10, 20 and 30 kb introns<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3044">27</a></sup>. <i>P</i>. <i>veris GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> shares this feature (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S4d</a>), as does <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Huu, C. N. et al. Presence versus absence of CYP734A50 underlies the style-length dimorphism in primroses. eLife 5, e17956 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3067">28</a></sup> (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S4d</a>). <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> introns &gt;5 kb (median 11,463.5 bp, n = 6) are in the top 5% of intron lengths genome-wide; the median genome-wide intron size is 440 bp (n = 133,334) (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S4c</a>). The median intron size in regions flanking the <i>S</i> locus is 351 bp (n = 91). The remaining introns, including both those &lt;5 kb in <i>PvGLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>PvCYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>, and those in <i>PvPUM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>, <i>PvKFB</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>PvCCM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>, are all &lt;1 kb (median 426.5 bp, n = 8) (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S4c,d</a>). There is greater intergenic distance (reduced gene density) between genes at the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris S</i> locus (10,925 bp, 103,811 bp, 17,438 bp, 13,307 bp; median 15,372.5 bp) (n = 4) compared to the flanking regions (median 1,816; n = 13), suggesting the absence of recombination might have impacted the genomic composition of the region.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec9" data-title="Discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec9-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec9">Discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec9-content"><p><i>Primula vulgaris</i> exhibits floral heteromorphy (heterostyly), with reciprocal positioning of the anthers and stigma (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig1">1a,b</a>), and an SI system that prevents fertilization from pollen of the same floral morph. Together, these adaptations increase allelic heterozygosity in obligate outcrossing pin and thrum plants, which complicates the assembly of genomic short sequencing reads<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Pryszcz, L. P. &amp; Gabaldón, T. Redundans: an assembly pipeline for highly heterozygous genomes. Nucleic Acids Research 44, e113 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3151">45</a></sup> in this species. For genome assembly, the low allelic diversity of a homozygous genome results in fewer conflicting sites, leading to increased contiguity and reduced numbers of fragmented gene models, duplicate redundant contigs and incorrectly predicted gene paralogues<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Pryszcz, L. P. &amp; Gabaldón, T. Redundans: an assembly pipeline for highly heterozygous genomes. Nucleic Acids Research 44, e113 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3155">45</a></sup>. For the genome asssembly of potato (<i>Solanum tuberosum</i>), a self-incompatible crop, the issue of heterozygosity was overcome using a homozygous doubled-monoploid derived through tissue culture<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Paz, M. M. &amp; Veilleux, R. E. Influence of culture medium and in vitro conditions on shoot regeneration in Solanum phureja monoploids and fertility of regenerated doubled monoploids. Plant Breeding 118, 53–57 (1999)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3162">46</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Xu, X. et al. Genome sequence and analysis of the tuber crop potato. Nature 475, 189–195 (2011)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3165">47</a></sup>. In some cases, assembly of a heterozygous genome is unavoidable; for example, <i>Trifolium pratense</i> (red clover) is difficult to inbreed without severe loss of viability and vigour<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="De Vega, J. J. et al. Red clover (Trifolium pratense L.) draft genome provides a platform for trait improvement. Scientific Reports 5, 17394 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3173">48</a></sup>. For <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i>, we sampled a self-fertile long homostyle plant from an inbred population that originates from Wyke Champflower in Somerset, UK<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Crosby, J. L. High proportions of homostyle plants in populations of Primula vulgaris. Nature 145, 672–673 (1940)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3183">31</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Crosby, J. L. Selection of an unfavourable gene complex. Evolutionary Ecology Research 3, 212–230 (1949)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3186">32</a></sup>. This highly homozygous individual allowed us to assemble the first <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> reference assembly of 411 Mb, which covers ~87% of the mean estimated 474 Mb genome<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Temsch, E. M., Temsch, W., Ehrendorfer-Schratt, L. &amp; Greilhuber, J. Heavy metal pollution, selection, and genome size: the species of the Žerjav study revisited with flow cytometry. Journal of Botany 2010, 596542 (2010)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3197">12</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Siljak-Yakovlev, S. et al. Towards a genome size and chromosome number database of Balkan flora: C-values in 343 taxa with novel values for 242. Advanced Science Letters 3, 190–213 (2010)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3200">13</a></sup>.</p><p>We previously identified the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris S</i> locus as the first complete structure of a heterostyly supergene; this region is hemizygous in thrum plants<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3213">27</a></sup>. Here, our comparative analyses indicate that the hemizygous genetic architecture of the <i>S</i> locus is conserved in the <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> thrum genome; furthermore, the five <i>S</i> locus genes identified in <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> are also present and show thrum-specific expression. Further analysis reveals reduced genomic read coverage across <i>S</i> locus coding sequence regions for <i>P</i>. <i>farinosa</i> (thrum), <i>P</i>. <i>forbesii</i> (thrum), and <i>P</i>. <i>scotica</i> (homostyle species) (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig5">5</a>), which would suggest the <i>S</i> locus is also absent from the pin chromosome in these species; however, due to phylogenetic distance this remains a hypothesis. Future mapping of genomic pin reads from distant species and PCR analysis across border sequences will confirm whether the <i>S</i> locus genetic architecture is conserved in the Primulaceae. <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3273">27</a></sup> and <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Huu, C. N. et al. Presence versus absence of CYP734A50 underlies the style-length dimorphism in primroses. eLife 5, e17956 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3282">28</a></sup> have nonetheless been identified as thrum-specific in a range of <i>Primula</i> species, which would support such a conclusion. Our previous estimate for the origin of the <i>S</i> locus using <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>GLO</i> sequences from six <i>Primula</i> species (including <i>P</i>. <i>farinosa</i>), is 51.7 MYA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3312">27</a></sup>. This age predates the divergence of the Primulaceae, and would be consistent with the apparent conservation of <i>S</i> locus genetic architecture, which would suggest a shared evolutionary history for heterostylous <i>Primula</i> species.</p><p>We annotated 24,599 genes in our <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> assembly. Our in-depth analysis of the <i>S</i> locus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3334">27</a></sup> revealed <i>CCM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> spans two contigs in the automated gene predictions; the gene number is therefore 24,598 if these two contigs are joined. The high percentage of RNA-Seq reads and CEGs mapping to the genome assembly suggests that most of the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> genespace has been captured in the assembly. Further searches for degenerate TE sequences revealed 762 of the predicted <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> genes are potentially TE-related, which could further reduce the total to 23,836. Conversely, these genes may encode endogenous proteins, as is the case with the AP2 binding domain that is present in both plant developmental transcription factors (TFs) and integrases such as tn916<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Balaji, S., Babu, M. M., Iyer, L. M. &amp; Aravind, L. Discovery of the principal specific transcription factors of Apicomplexa and their implication for the evolution of the AP2-integrase DNA binding domains. Nucleic Acids Research 33, 3994–4006 (2005)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3357">49</a></sup>. Recruitment of TF binding domains from transposases or integrases is a potentially recurrent theme in evolution<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Balaji, S., Babu, M. M., Iyer, L. M. &amp; Aravind, L. Discovery of the principal specific transcription factors of Apicomplexa and their implication for the evolution of the AP2-integrase DNA binding domains. Nucleic Acids Research 33, 3994–4006 (2005)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3361">49</a></sup>, resulting in evolutionary mobile protein domains in different sequence contexts<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Triant, D. A. &amp; Pearson, W. R. Most partial domains in proteins are alignment and annotation artifacts. Genome biology 16, 99 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3366">50</a></sup>. OrthoMCL analysis of <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> genes and their orthologues in four angiosperm species (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S3</a>) reveals <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> as a paralogue of <i>GLO</i> in <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> as expected<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3395">27</a></sup>, within a group containing MADS-box like genes in rice and tomato, as well as <i>PISTILATTA</i> from Arabidopsis. OrthoMCL did not identify paralogues for the remaining four <i>S</i> locus genes due to partial hits of low similarity, perhaps suggesting the duplication<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3406">27</a></sup> of <i>GLO</i> to <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> represents the most recent ancestral step in assembly of the <i>S</i> locus supergene; we note, however, that <i>CCM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> does have sequence similarity (~90%) with another gene elsewhere in the genome<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3429">27</a></sup>. Further investigation of the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> genome to analyse gene families related to the <i>S</i> locus cluster will help to establish the ancestral steps leading to heterostyly.</p><p><i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> and <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> are both heterostylous, closely-related, and can interbreed to produce hybrids known as “false oxlip”<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Gurney, M., Preston, C., Barrett, J. &amp; Briggs, D. Hybridisation between oxlip Primula elatior (L.) Hill and primrose P. vulgaris Hudson, and the identification of their variable hybrid P. x digenea A. Kerner. Watsonia 26, 239–252 (2007)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3456">51</a></sup>. The two species have similarly-sized diploid genomes (<i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> = 479 Mb; <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> = 474 Mb)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Siljak-Yakovlev, S. et al. Towards a genome size and chromosome number database of Balkan flora: C-values in 343 taxa with novel values for 242. Advanced Science Letters 3, 190–213 (2010)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3473">13</a></sup>, and might be expected to contain a similar number of genes. However, the reported <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> genome assembly has 18,301 annotated genes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3484">14</a></sup> (<i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> = 24,599). To determine whether this represents a true difference in gene count, we compared coding sequences. We show a reduced percentage of mapped RNA-Seq reads and an absence of <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> genes in the <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> genome and annotations. This difference could result from use of RNA-Seq datasets from a broader range of <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> tissues in the current study (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S2</a>). For genes absent from the assembly, the highly-polymorphic <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> read library, which combines genomic DNA from the heterozygous genomes of both a pin and a thrum plant<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3523">14</a></sup> would result in difficulties assembling the <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> genome due to the presence of four haplotypes. The higher <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> contig size cut-off (&lt;888 bp)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3539">14</a></sup> (vs. &lt;200 bp for <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i>) may also have removed true genomic content. In addition, the number of transcripts found in the reported <i>P</i>. <i>veris de novo</i> transcriptome assembly was much greater (25,409) than the number of predicted genes in the partial <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> assembly<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3563">14</a></sup>; although <i>de novo</i> transcriptomes often contain inflated numbers of transcripts<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Sayadi, A., Immonen, E., Bayram, H. &amp; Arnqvist, G. The de novo transcriptome and its functional annotation in the seed beetle Callosobruchus maculatus. Plos One 11, e0158565 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3570">52</a></sup>, this perhaps suggests there are more genes in the <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> genome than present in the genome-guided gene predictions for this species<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3580">14</a></sup>. These results suggest the different number of annotated genes is due to a greater percentage of genes captured in the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> LH_v2 assembly and gene predictions, rather than inherent differences between the two species; ~24,000 genes is perhaps a reasonable estimate for the true gene number in these closely-related species.</p><p>Genes differentially expressed between pin and thrum flowers show over-representation of GO terms potentially relating to reproductive processes, and pathways that might affect cell wall modification in the development of dimorphic <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> flowers (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig3">3c</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Webster, M. A. &amp; Gilmartin, P. M. Analysis of late stage flower development in Primula vulgaris reveals novel differences in cell morphology and temporal aspects of floral heteromorphy. New Phytologist 171, 591–603 (2006)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3604">53</a></sup>. Low expression for <i>S</i> locus genes other than <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> compared to the differentially expressed geneset (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S5</a>) would be consistent with roles as master regulators that control groups of more highly expressed genes, through the modulation of phytohormones for example<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3621">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Huu, C. N. et al. Presence versus absence of CYP734A50 underlies the style-length dimorphism in primroses. eLife 5, e17956 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3624">28</a></sup>, which are often produced in low concentrations<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Wani, S. H., Kumar, V., Shriram, V. &amp; Sah, S. K. Phytohormones and their metabolic engineering for abiotic stress tolerance in crop plants. The Crop Journal 4, 162–176 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3628">54</a></sup>. Future detailed temporal analyses will determine <i>S</i> locus gene expression throughout flower development, and further our understanding of the dynamic action of these regulators on genome-wide gene expression. The <i>Primula S</i> locus was predicted to either contain, or be in close linkage with, genes encoding molecular specificities that determine SI<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Barrett, S. &amp; Shore, J. In Self-Incompatibility in Flowering Plants: Evolution, Diversity and Mechanisms (ed V. E. Franklin-Tong) 3–32 (Springer, 2008)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3639">9</a></sup>, based on the loss of SI in homostyle plants assumed to arise from recombination between dominant and recessive <i>S</i> alleles<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lewis, D. Comparative incompatibility in angiosperms and fungi. Advances in Genetics Incorporating Molecular Genetic Medicine 6, 235–285 (1954)." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3646">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lewis, D. &amp; Jones, D. A. In Evolution and Function of Heterostyly (ed. Barrett, S. C. H.) 129–150 (Springer Verlag, 1992)." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3646_1">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Dowrick, V. P. J. Heterostyly and homostyly in Primula obconica. Heredity 10, 219–236 (1956)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3649">6</a></sup>. The <i>Primula S</i> (<i>Style length</i>) locus is distinct from the <i>S</i> loci defined in homomorphic self-incompatible species<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hiscock, S. J. &amp; Tabah, D. A. The different mechanisms of sporophytic self-incompatibility. Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society B 358, 1037-1045 (2003)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3663">11</a></sup>; unlike homomorphic-SI <i>S</i> loci, the finding that the <i>Primula</i> thrum <i>S</i> locus haplotype has no counterpart in pin with which to recombine<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3676">27</a></sup>, together with the observation that <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> mutations not only result in homostyle flowers, but also self-compatibility<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3693">27</a></sup>, raises the possibility that the SI determinants associated with heterostyly might be present in the large differentially expressed geneset, under the control of <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>, rather than located at the <i>S</i> locus itself. The existence of homozygous <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> homostyle plants such as the Somerset and Chiltern long homostyles, which are diploid for the <i>S</i> locus gene cluster<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3723">27</a></sup> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig5">5</a>), highlights a further question to be resolved on the proposed recessive lethal gene linked to the <i>S</i> locus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Kurian, V. &amp; Richards, A. A new recombinant in the heteromorphy “S” supergene in Primula. Heredity 78, 383–390 (1997)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3733">55</a></sup>, suggested as the basis for preventing homozygous thrums. These plants are the result of mutation, not recombination, which suggests SI is the key, very effective, mechanism that prevents homozygous (<i>S</i>/<i>S</i>) thrum plants from occurring<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Kurian, V. &amp; Richards, A. A new recombinant in the heteromorphy “S” supergene in Primula. Heredity 78, 383–390 (1997)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3744">55</a></sup>.</p><p>Our analyses reveal the number of genes with significantly higher expression in thrum is double the number with significantly higher expression in pin (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig3">3a</a>). The thrum-specific <i>S</i> locus alters pin floral architecture by reducing cell length in the style, increasing cell division below the point of anther attachment, modifying cell morphology in the upper corolla tube, and increasing pollen size<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Webster, M. A. &amp; Gilmartin, P. M. Analysis of late stage flower development in Primula vulgaris reveals novel differences in cell morphology and temporal aspects of floral heteromorphy. New Phytologist 171, 591–603 (2006)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3757">53</a></sup>. These findings appear to suggest that the upregulation of a greater number of genes is required for development of a more complex set of thrum-specific traits. Refining these intricate developmental events in thrum most likely requires modulated expression of genes required in both pin and thrum flowers to bring about change from the default pin architecture, whilst maintaining a flower of the same overall size. Surprisingly, only eight genes with morph-specific expression (expressed uniquely in either pin or thrum) (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig3">3b</a>) are expressed at a significant level (including <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>); there are no significantly enriched GO terms in this geneset (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S6</a>). Genes controlled by the <i>S</i> locus could be required for default floral development, and are therefore present and expressed in both pin and thrum. These genes might be differentially expressed rather than morph-specific in expression due to the modification of floral architecture rather than generation of novel structure, enabling fine-scale tuning to maintain overall flower size in the two floral morphs.</p><p><i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> LH_v2 annotations generated in this study allowed us to investigate repeat sequences in the <i>S</i> locus region (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S4</a>), with analyses revealing elevated TE sequence content (64%) compared to genome-wide (37%). This feature may be due to proximity of the <i>S</i> locus to the centromere<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Li, J. et al. Integration of genetic and physical maps of the Primula vulgaris S locus and localization by chromosome in situ hybridisation. New Phytologist 208, 137–148 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3794">26</a></sup>, a chromosomal region with characteristically high repeat content<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Lamb, J. C. &amp; Birchler, J. A. The role of DNA sequence in centromere formation. Genome biology 4, 214 (2003)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3799">56</a></sup>. However, we reveal a remarkable contrast in the TE content of sequences immediately flanking the <i>S</i> locus (34%) in comparison to the <i>S</i> locus itself (64%), suggesting the elevated repeat content is not simply due to chromosomal location. TEs and insertional mutations can accumulate in regions with reduced recombination<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Rizzon, C., Marais, G., Gouy, M. &amp; Biémont, C. Recombination rate and the distribution of transposable elements in the Drosophila melanogaster genome. Genome Research 12, 400–407 (2002)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3809">57</a></sup>, with a build-up of mutations potentially rendering a TE incapable of transposing. Since hemizygosity of the <i>S</i> locus in thrums precludes homologous recombination, the efficiency of selection would be reduced by restricting fixation of favourable allele combinations at linked loci<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Comeron, J. M., Williford, A. &amp; Kliman, R. M. The Hill-Robertson effect: evolutionary consequences of weak selection and linkage in finite populations. Heredity 100, 19–31 (2007)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3816">58</a></sup>. The resulting build-up of deleterious mutations hitchhiking with beneficial mutations could lead to TE insertion without selective constraints, and larger introns; in some eukaryotes, a negative correlation of intron length with recombination rate has been observed<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Comeron, J. M. &amp; Kreitman, M. The correlation between intron length and recombination in Drosophila: dynamic equilibrium between mutational and selective forces. Genetics 156, 1175–1190 (2000)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3821">44</a></sup>. We note the presence of large introns and intergenic gaps in the <i>S</i> locus region compared to both the flanking regions and genome-wide (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S4c</a>). Reduced efficiency of selection as a result of decreased recombination rate has also been linked to short introns that are less than the minimum intron length required for the intron splicing reaction, defined as &lt;80–90 bp in <i>Drosophila</i> studies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Comeron, J. M. &amp; Kreitman, M. The correlation between intron length and recombination in Drosophila: dynamic equilibrium between mutational and selective forces. Genetics 156, 1175–1190 (2000)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3834">44</a></sup>. However, the remaining introns, including those in <i>PUM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>, whilst noticeably smaller than the remarkably large (&gt;5 kb) introns in <i>GLO</i><sup><i>T</i></sup> and <i>CYP</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>, have sizes (median 426.5 bp) in line with the genome-wide average;  two of the <i>S</i> locus genes (<i>KFB</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>, <i>CCM</i><sup><i>T</i></sup>) have no introns.</p><p>The characterisation of the supergene controlling butterfly mimicry, as a single gene preserved in linkage disequilibrium by a chromosomal inversion<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Kunte, K. et al. Doublesex is a mimicry supergene. Nature 507, 229–232 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3876">59</a></sup>, is in stark contrast to the multiple gene <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris S</i> locus region. Despite suppression of recombination, gene conversion events and rare multiple crossovers are still possible between standard and inverted chromosomes (inversion heterozygotes)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Hoffmann, A. A., Sgrò, C. M. &amp; Weeks, A. R. Chromosomal inversion polymorphisms and adaptation. Trends in Ecology &amp; Evolution 19, 482–488 (2004)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3886">60</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Davey, J. W. et al. No evidence for maintenance of a sympatric Heliconius species barrier by chromosomal inversions. Evolution Letters 1, 138–154 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3889">61</a></sup>. For hemizygous <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> thrum plants, there is no opportunity for genetic exchange within the <i>S</i> locus supergene, due to the absence of the region from the pin chromosome. In hemizygous regions of the Y chromosome in humans, the presence of large, near-identical (&gt;99.9% sequence identity) palindromic repeats that encompass the male-specific genes is well documented<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Rozen, S. et al. Abundant gene conversion between arms of palindromes in human and ape Y chromosomes. Nature 423, 873–876 (2003)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3903">62</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Bachtrog, D. Y chromosome evolution: emerging insights into processes of Y chromosome degeneration. Nature reviews. Genetics 14, 113–124 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3906">63</a></sup>. These repeats could be maintained by intra-chromosomal gene conversion, to facilitate the restoration of deleterious mutations by replacement with mutation-free gene copies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Rozen, S. et al. Abundant gene conversion between arms of palindromes in human and ape Y chromosomes. Nature 423, 873–876 (2003)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3910">62</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Bachtrog, D. Y chromosome evolution: emerging insights into processes of Y chromosome degeneration. Nature reviews. Genetics 14, 113–124 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3913">63</a></sup>. However, for the <i>Primula S</i> locus, the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> genome assembly reveals no near-identical repeated sequences or remarkably similar genes elsewhere in the genome.</p><p>Our findings suggest that the thrum-specific architecture of the <i>Primula</i> <i>S</i> locus is an evolutionary-conserved feature. In addition to functional analysis of the <i>S</i> locus genes and downstream pathways, this indicates that future investigations into the evolution of the region, including how its function is maintained given the above observations, will be the next big challenge to understand the <i>S</i> locus in Darwin’s primroses. The <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> genome assembly will, alongside the fully characterized <i>S</i> locus region, provide the resources to facilitate this research.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec10" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec10-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec10">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec10-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Genome assembly</h3><p>SOAPdenovo v2.04<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Luo, R. et al. SOAPdenovo2: an empirically improved memory-efficient short-read de novo assembler. Gigascience 1, 1–6 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3964">36</a></sup> was used to assemble contigs using genomic paired-end reads (Illumina HiSeq 2500) from an individual <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> long homostyle (Somerset) plant (-K 81); reads were generated as described previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Cocker, J. et al. Oakleaf: an S locus-linked mutation of Primula vulgaris that affects leaf and flower development. New Phytologist 208, 149–161 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3974">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3977">27</a></sup> (Supplementary Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>–<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S3</a>). Contigs were scaffolded with paired-end reads, then mate-pair libraries, in order of ascending insert size (5, 7 and 9 kb; Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>) (−k 41); ≥5 links required to join contigs into a scaffold (pair_num_cutoff=5), contigs &lt;100 bp excluded (-L 100). SOAP GapCloser was used to fill gaps in scaffolds (rd_len_cutof=70, map_len=35). BLASTN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 1–9 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d1397e3991">64</a></sup> was used to identify and remove non-<i>Primula</i> contigs based on alignments to the NCBI “nr” database (≥90% identity; ≥50% coverage; alignment length ≥100 bp), and also additional <i>Primula</i> chloroplast sequences from <i>Primula sinensis</i> (KU321892.1), <i>Primula poissonii</i> (KF753634.1), and <i>Primula veris</i> (KX639823.1). Removal of contaminate contigs and contigs &lt;200 bp produced the final assembly (LH_v2). To assess completeness and duplicated content in the assembly, <i>k</i>-mer hashes were generated for the paired-end reads and scaffolds using Jellyfish v2.2.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Marçais, G. &amp; Kingsford, C. A fast, lock-free approach for efficient parallel counting of occurrences of k-mers. Bioinformatics 27, 764–770 (2011)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4014">65</a></sup>, and compared with the K-mer Analysis Toolkit<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Mapleson, D., Garcia Accinelli, G., Kettleborough, G., Wright, J. &amp; Clavijo, B. J. KAT: a K-mer analysis toolkit to quality control NGS datasets and genome assemblies. Bioinformatics 33, 574–576 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4018">34</a></sup>. The proportion of <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> RNA-Seq reads, transcripts, and core eukaryotic genes mapping to the assembly was also evaluated (Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>). Draft assembly of paired-end reads from an individual <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> thrum plant (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>) (VT_v1) was performed with ABySS v1.3.4 (<i>k</i> = 81)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Simpson, J. T. et al. ABySS: a parallel assembler for short read sequence data. Genome Research 19, 1117–1123 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4045">66</a></sup>; this assembly was not annotated.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Genome annotation</h3><p>RepeatModeler (open v1.0.7) (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/RepeatModeler.html">http://www.repeatmasker.org/RepeatModeler.html</a>) was used to identify <i>de novo</i> repeat sequences in the LH_v2 assembly. These sequences were curated as described in Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>. LH_v2 was annotated using the <i>de novo</i> repeat library with RepeatMasker (open v4.0.1; RMBlast v2.2.27) (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>); additional classification of repeat elements was performed with TEclass v2.1.3<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Abrusan, G., Grundmann, N., DeMester, L. &amp; Makalowski, W. TEclass—a tool for automated classification of unknown eukaryotic transposable elements. Bioinformatics 25, 1329–1330 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4081">67</a></sup>.</p><p>To generate a training set of genes for the eukaryotic gene-prediction software AUGUSTUS v2.7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Stanke, M., Diekhans, M., Baertsch, R. &amp; Haussler, D. Using native and syntenically mapped cDNA alignments to improve de novo gene finding. Bioinformatics 24, 637–644 (2008)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4088">68</a></sup>, RNA-Seq reads from leaves, flowers, seed, seedlings, and roots (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S2</a>) were aligned to LH_v2 with TopHat v2.0.11<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Kim, D. et al. TopHat2: accurate alignment of transcriptomes in the presence of insertions, deletions and gene fusions. Genome biology 14, 1–13 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4095">69</a></sup>. Transcripts from all libraries were assembled and merged using Cufflinks v2.1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Differential gene and transcript expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with TopHat and Cufflinks. Nature Protocols 7, 562–578 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4099">70</a></sup>, then filtered with full_lengther_next (<a href="https://rubygems.org/gems/full_lengther_next/">https://rubygems.org/gems/full_lengther_next/</a>) to identify full-length transcripts, and remove overlapping transcripts. AUGUSTUS was trained using 2,000 transcripts and the training parameters assessed with an additional 200 genes. In addition to <i>de novo</i> repeat annotations (“--nolow” and “--norna” RepeatMasker options applied), evidence sets based on protein, cDNA, and RNA-Seq intron and exon positions, were generated for gene prediction (Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>).</p><p>Once trained, AUGUSTUS was used to identify genes in LH_v2 scaffolds. RNA-Seq reads from all libraries were aligned to scaffolds using AUGUSTUS predictions as “known transcripts” (-G parameter), then Cufflinks v2.1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Differential gene and transcript expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with TopHat and Cufflinks. Nature Protocols 7, 562–578 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4120">70</a></sup> used to assemble transcripts. PASA2 April 25-2013 beta release<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the Program to Assemble Spliced Alignments. Genome biology 9, R7 (2008)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4124">71</a></sup> was used to generate a modified annotation from these alignments; another round of alignment, assembly and correction was performed to generate final gene models. Functional annotation and identification of GO-terms and domains associated with the predicted genes was performed with AHRD<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Hallab, A. Protein Function Prediction Using Phylogenomics, Domain Architecture Analysis, Data Integration, and Lexical Scoring. (PhD thesis, Universitäts-und Landesbibliothek Bonn, 2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4128">72</a></sup>, Blast2GO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Conesa, A. et al. Blast2GO: a universal tool for annotation, visualization and analysis in functional genomics research. Bioinformatics 21, 3674–3676 (2005)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4132">73</a></sup>, and InterProScan5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Jones, P. et al. InterProScan 5: genome-scale protein function classification. Bioinformatics 30, 1236–1240 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4136">74</a></sup> (Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">
                           <i>Primula</i> gene comparison and expression</h3><p><i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> and <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4166">14</a></sup> coding sequences (CDSs) were aligned against each other, and to the <i>P. veris</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4172">14</a></sup> and <i>P. vulgaris</i> LH_v2 genome assemblies, using TBLASTX v2.2.31<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 1–9 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4180">64</a></sup>. High Scoring Pairs (HSPs) with ≥95% sequence identity were extracted; total percentage coverage across each CDS was recorded, and the cumulative number of CDSs with each coverage plotted for each of the four alignments using R v3.2.0 (<a href="https://www.r-project.org/">https://www.r-project.org/</a>). OrthoMCL v2.0.9<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Li, L. OrthoMCL: Identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Research 13, 2178–2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4191">75</a></sup> was used to find orthologous and paralogous gene groups based on all-vs-all alignments between proteins from <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i>, <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i>, and other angiosperm species (Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>).</p><p>RNA-Seq reads were generated in biological-replicate from 15–20 mm buds of four pin and four thrum <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> plants (siblings) (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S3</a>), as described previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4223">27</a></sup>. Differential expression analysis with Cufflinks v2.1.1 Cuffdiff <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Differential analysis of gene regulation at transcript resolution with RNA-seq. Nature Biotechnology 31, 46–53 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4227">76</a></sup>, and GO term enrichment analysis with goatools (<a href="https://github.com/tanghaibao/goatools">https://github.com/tanghaibao/goatools</a>), was performed (Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>).</p><p><i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris S</i> locus genes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4250">27</a></sup> were defined in the published <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> GFF file of predicted genes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4260">14</a></sup> (Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>). Public RNA-Seq reads for <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> pin and thrum flower RNA (BioProject PRJNA238546)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Nowak, M. D. et al. The draft genome of Primula veris yields insight into the molecular basis of heterostyly. Genome biology 16, 16 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4274">14</a></sup> (no replicates), and <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> style and corolla tube RNA prepared from pin and thrum flowers (pooled from 25 plants)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Huu, C. N. et al. Presence versus absence of CYP734A50 underlies the style-length dimorphism in primroses. eLife 5, e17956 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4285">28</a></sup> (BioProject PRJNA317964) were aligned to the published <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> genome, prior to differential expression analysis (Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>). PCR analysis of <i>S</i> locus genes was performed on cDNA from <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> and <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> mixed-stage flower buds using the method described previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4314">27</a></sup>; primers and amplification conditions listed in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S7</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">
                           <i>Primula S</i> locus genomic read coverage</h3><p>LH_v2 contigs forming the <i>S</i> locus region generated previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Li, J. et al. Genetic architecture and evolution of the S locus supergene in Primula vulgaris. Nature Plants 2, 16188 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4336">27</a></sup> were removed from the <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> assembly and replaced with the contiguous 455,880 bp <i>S</i> locus and flanking sequences. BWA v0.7.12<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754–1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4350">77</a></sup> “aln” was used to map genomic reads from <i>P</i>. <i>veris</i> thrum, and <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> thrum and pin (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>) to this assembly. SAMtools v0.1.19<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Li, H. et al. The Sequence Alignment/Map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078–2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4370">78</a></sup> “depth” was used to compute read depth across the 455 kb region (Q30), which was normalized according to library size and plotted in 5 kb windows (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig4">4a</a>) with R v3.2.0 (<a href="https://www.r-project.org/">https://www.r-project.org/</a>). BWA v0.7.2 “mem”<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Li, H. Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. arXiv 1303.3997 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4384">79</a></sup> and Samtools v1.1.19<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Li, H. et al. The Sequence Alignment/Map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078–2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d1397e4388">78</a></sup> were used for mapping and finding the depth of coverage of genomic reads from <i>Primula</i> species across predicted <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> LH_v2 <i>S</i> locus coding sequence positions (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#Fig5">5</a>) (Supplementary Methods <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-018-36304-4#MOESM1">S1</a>).</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data Availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data Availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>Sequencing data are available under BioProject PRJEB9683, PRJNA260472, PRJEB21011, GenBank accessions MF317487 to MF317489, and <a href="http://opendata.earlham.ac.uk/primula">http://opendata.earlham.ac.uk/primula</a>.</p>

J.W. generated the final <i>P</i>. <i>vulgaris</i> assembly, generated evidence for gene prediction, carried out genome assembly validation and gene prediction, and contributed to the manuscript text and project design. J.L. prepared all DNA and RNA samples for sequencing, contributed to curation of gene annotations, carried out and prepared figures for PCR expression analyses, contributed to manuscript text and coordinated the project. S.D., D.S. and M.C. contributed to project design, including the sequencing and genome annotation strategy. P.M.G. contributed to figures and the manuscript text, designed and directed the project, and carried out manuscript revision; all authors read and approved the final manuscript, and contributed to manuscript editing.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding author</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to

Gilmartin</a>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="ethics" data-title="Ethics declarations"><div class="c-article-section" id="ethics-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="ethics">Ethics declarations</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="ethics-content">

            </li>
